## Section 001: Mern Typescript Stack Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Mern Typescript Stack Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names the stack but does not state that the reference owns cross-layer contract, state, API, persistence, security, and operational decisions rather than generic framework tutorials
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Mern Typescript Stack Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because MERN failures often arise between layers where compile-time types disappear, client validation is untrusted, database semantics differ from DTOs, and retries or caches can repeat side effects
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Mern Typescript Stack Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the task is GraphQL-first, WebSocket-heavy, queue-dominant, sharded or multi-region, search-heavy, or a modern meta-framework changes the server/client execution model beyond classic MERN assumptions
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Mern Typescript Stack Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this reference for classic REST-style React, Express, Mongoose, and MongoDB work with TypeScript; route architectural variants and specialized distributed concerns elsewhere
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Mern Typescript Stack Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add an opening cross-layer operating contract, task classifier, trust-boundary sequence, explicit exclusions, and repository-backed completion evidence
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Mern Typescript Stack Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that full-stack type safety is a chain of independently verified runtime contracts, not a single shared TypeScript interface; every serialization or persistence boundary must re-establish trust

## Section 002: Source Evidence Mapping Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed separates four local paths from three public sources but gives every local file the same generic usage role and does not reveal that two doctrine files are byte-identical or that one library is historical
- **supporting_reason:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because source-role precision prevents duplicate evidence from inflating confidence and keeps old code examples or unopened URLs from being presented as current ecosystem contracts
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: duplicate doctrine paths are counted as two authorities, historical package snippets become current defaults, public links are cited as read, or TypeScript documentation is stretched into Express or database behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this table to route and label evidence, not to certify current APIs or replace target code, configuration, and tests
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add exact local roles, duplicate detection, historical-code safeguards, uninspected external state, and a claim-level evidence record
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that an evidence map is a deduplicated provenance graph; confidence should follow independent and applicable observations, not the number of paths that repeat the same prose

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed says local-first, public-second, verification-backed synthesis but does not state the full-stack reliability thesis or reconcile the frontend-oriented journey with backend operating guidance
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because TypeScript types are erased at runtime and cannot by themselves protect JSON, tokens, query strings, database documents, local storage, or concurrent writes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: a shared interface is treated as validation, the frontend journey is optimized without backend invariants, the backend model ignores user loading and error recovery, or historical snippets override current repository behavior
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply this thesis to classic REST-style MERN implementations and reviews, not as a complete doctrine for GraphQL, real-time, or distributed data systems
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to replace generic synthesis with an erased-types trust-boundary thesis, reconcile frontend and backend outcomes, and require a complete user-to-database trace
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that reliability compounds multiplicatively across boundaries: a strong layer cannot compensate for an unvalidated handoff, while small explicit checks at every transition create end-to-end confidence

- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat each layer as an independent trust and ownership boundary: validate unknown input at runtime, map distinct DTO and entity shapes, keep server and client state separate, centralize failures, make database semantics explicit, and test the same transport and persistence paths users exercise

## Section 010: User Journey Scenario
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed describes only a frontend product engineer choosing components and visual states, which conflicts with the same file's backend service workload and omits the Express, Mongoose, MongoDB, auth, and operations path
- **supporting_reason:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a frontend-only journey can look polished while the API trusts malformed input or corrupts concurrent data, and a backend-only journey can be correct while leaving users trapped in stale loading or unrecoverable error states
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the journey spans multiple services or irreversible migration, auth policy is undecided, UI state and API state have competing owners, or a real-time architecture exceeds this reference
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use the journey for one coherent product capability; split cross-service, real-time, or migration-heavy work by ownership and rollback
- **revision_decision:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to reconcile the frontend-only seed with a full client-to-database journey, enumerate principal states and invariants, and require end-to-end evidence
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 010 "User Journey Scenario", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the user journey is the smallest end-to-end consistency proof: each visible state should correspond to a stable backend outcome and each side effect should have a user-observable completion or recovery

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed offers generic adopt, adapt, avoid, and cost-of-error rows but does not compare the stack's recurring choices about contracts, state, writes, reads, modeling, pagination, auth, and retries
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because some defaults are low-cost safety floors, while persistence and security choices encode workload and threat assumptions that cannot be selected from syntax alone
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: adoption perpetuates an unsafe convention, adaptation spreads conditional logic across layers, avoidance is based on trend, or cost of error is noted without deeper review
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply this guide to bounded classic MERN choices; use dedicated architecture, threat-modeling, and migration processes for broader changes
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add concrete cross-layer choice pairs, distinguish safety floors from contextual decisions, and scale evidence by irreversibility
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the cost of being wrong follows irreversibility and hidden coupling more than code size; a one-line database or token decision can demand more evidence than an entire UI refactor

## Section 012: Local Corpus Hierarchy
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed assigns canonical, legacy, supporting, and historical roles, but it calls a byte-identical doctrine copy supporting detail and does not explain why the lightweight skill is legacy or how repository evidence overrides archive guidance
- **supporting_reason:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because content identity and functional role are more reliable hierarchy signals than path date alone, while live repository evidence is closer to the system being changed
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: canonical means universally current, the duplicate becomes a second vote, legacy code silently wins through detail, or target conventions override reliability without preserving the protected invariant
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use the hierarchy for this archive corpus and initial routing, never to displace live ownership or current security and dependency evidence automatically
- **revision_decision:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add content-hash deduplication, functional roles, explicit override order, conflict records, and invariant-preserving exception rules
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 012 "Local Corpus Hierarchy", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that hierarchy is an override protocol, not a prestige ranking; reliable evolution depends on knowing when a nearer observation may replace a broader source without losing its invariant

## Section 016: Completeness Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: boxes are checked from intention, build success substitutes for runtime validation, UI-only evidence drives data changes, non-applicable hides an unowned concern, or the checklist replaces expert review
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use the full checklist for implementation and release guidance, with justified reduced scope for narrowly editorial work
- **revision_decision:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain all seven seed bullets, add full-stack technical and release evidence, require non-applicability rationale, and finish with connected journey replay
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that completeness is a graph property: all required artifacts must connect through consistent contracts and ownership, not merely exist in isolation
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 016 "Completeness Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to require a bounded workflow, source and repository evidence, runtime request schemas, distinct contract and entity shapes, client state ownership, authorization, service invariant, query or write semantics, model and index fit, stable responses, user success and failure states, tests across affected boundaries, observability, uncertainty, rollout, rollback, and adjacent routes

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed calls this a backend operating reference and proposes one service, 25 endpoints or workers, 1000 requests, and one rollback, but the title and journey also cover React and those numbers lack calibration
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because coherent contracts and reversibility matter more than endpoint count; a small route can be high risk when it changes auth or data, while many simple reads may share one safe boundary
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the batch spans services or teams, 1000 sequential requests stand in for load, endpoints mix unrelated hotspots, UI and API contracts migrate separately, schema changes are irreversible, or real-time and queue behavior enters scope
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this model for task decomposition and representative verification, not production capacity certification
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to reconcile frontend and backend scope, demote numeric values to prompts, center contract and rollback coherence, and add concurrency, schema, and data-reversibility dimensions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the right scope unit is the independently reversible contract graph, joining user behavior to data side effects and deployment ownership
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to scope a review batch to one independently owned user capability whose React workflow, API routes, service invariants, Mongo collections, and rollback can be traced together; use the seed endpoint and request numbers as split prompts rather than capacity guarantees
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because coherent contracts and reversibility matter more than endpoint count; a small route can be high risk when it changes auth or data, while many simple reads may share one safe boundary
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the batch spans services or teams, 1000 sequential requests stand in for load, endpoints mix unrelated hotspots, UI and API contracts migrate separately, schema changes are irreversible, or real-time and queue behavior enters scope

## Section 019: Reliability Target
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed sets provenance, 18-of-20 routing, unsupported-claim, and recovery targets but does not connect them to runtime contracts, user recovery, data integrity, or severity
- **supporting_reason:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a well-sourced document can still yield unsafe code if the target repository contradicts its assumptions, while runtime tests without provenance can institutionalize accidental behavior
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: 18-of-20 is universalized, two dangerous data or auth misses are averaged away, labels are decorative, or document pass status is called a service objective
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use these targets to assess reference decisions and their evidence packets, not to certify a deployed MERN service
- **revision_decision:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain all four rows, add severity and boundary sampling, link corpus gates to target tests, and prevent aggregate results from masking harmful errors
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 019 "Reliability Target", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that reliability error costs are asymmetric: one silent data corruption or authorization bypass outweighs several benign routing disagreements

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed covers source drift, generic advice, request surges, and security failure but includes coroutine language from another backend theme and omits MERN-specific diagnostic classes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because generic timeout or error labels lead to harmful recovery; diagnosis must identify whether load, retries, queries, writes, middleware, or client state caused the observed symptom
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: all timeouts trigger retry, validation errors reach the database, client cache masks failed writes, security is reduced to shape validation, or mitigation changes schema without compatibility and rollback
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this table for design and controlled verification; follow service incident and security procedures in production
- **revision_decision:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to reconcile the misplaced coroutine wording, expand into MERN diagnostic classes, and require containment plus original-trigger recovery proof
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that failure modes should partition recovery decisions; if two modes require opposing actions, telemetry must distinguish them before automation responds
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify failures by stale evidence, runtime schema breach, cache or UI reconciliation, async error propagation, event-loop blocking, write validation or concurrency, query and index shape, over-population, auth and secret handling, retry duplication, dependency saturation, readiness, and rollback
- **supporting_reason:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because generic timeout or error labels lead to harmful recovery; diagnosis must identify whether load, retries, queries, writes, middleware, or client state caused the observed symptom
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; all timeouts trigger retry, validation errors reach the database, client cache masks failed writes, security is reduced to shape validation, or mitigation changes schema without compatibility and rollback
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 020 "Failure Mode Table", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: use this table for design and controlled verification; follow service incident and security procedures in production

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed gives evidence-workflow retry and agent backpressure rules but does not separate browser query retries, Express admission, downstream clients, MongoDB transaction helpers, queues, or write idempotency
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because independent retry defaults in TanStack Query, HTTP clients, Express services, and transaction helpers multiply attempts and can create duplicate writes, stale feedback, and cascading load
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: validation or auth errors retry, POST writes have no key, an ambiguous timeout is treated as failure, transaction callbacks contain parallel unsupported work, browsers retry after logout, or backpressure exists only after MongoDB saturation
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: apply these principles through target-repository libraries and service policy rather than inventing a universal retry implementation
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to separate evidence and runtime layers, assign one retry owner, add idempotency and ambiguous-outcome handling, and share a capacity budget across the stack
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that retry and backpressure form one distributed budget across browser, API, and database; configuring layers independently creates invisible amplification
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify the failing layer; keep the seed's single evidence-refresh retry; retry runtime operations only for transient failures within deadlines and budgets; make writes idempotent or deduplicated; avoid nested retries; bound client, server, and database concurrency; and stop admission or rollout when downstream saturation or verification is red
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because independent retry defaults in TanStack Query, HTTP clients, Express services, and transaction helpers multiply attempts and can create duplicate writes, stale feedback, and cascading load

- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: separate evidence and runtime layers, assign one retry owner, add idempotency and ambiguous-outcome handling, and share a capacity budget across the stack

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed records source use, commands, percentiles, errors, retries, saturation, rollback, and compact evidence, but it does not connect browser workflows to Express request context, Mongo operations, and data outcomes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the same user-visible failure can arise from stale cache, middleware rejection, event-loop blocking, connection exhaustion, collection scan, write conflict, or retry amplification
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: tokens or request bodies are logged, dynamic IDs become metric labels, success emits before durable write, browser and server traces cannot join, or alerts have no owner and containment
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: define required semantics here and implement them with the repository's established telemetry and privacy controls
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to map generic signals onto the full workflow, add redaction and cardinality, verify failure-path emission, and tie every alert to a response
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that observability is a contract boundary: it must preserve enough semantic identity to join layers while deliberately dropping secrets and high-cardinality payload details
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed combines fallback p95 under 200 milliseconds and p99 under 500 milliseconds with UI workflow and layout signals but supplies no workload, environment, concurrency, query, render, or calibration details
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a fast API can still render poorly, a responsive UI can hide duplicate requests, and median request latency can stay flat while unindexed tails or event-loop blocking destroy capacity
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the 200/500 values become product objectives, 1000 sequential mocked calls prove scale, local hardware numbers are generalized, UI screenshots prove responsiveness, or throughput and errors are omitted
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use this method to design target-specific evidence, not to compare React, Express, Mongoose, or MongoDB abstractly
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to retain the seed values as provisional text, add end-to-end workload controls and query evidence, prioritize baseline deltas and saturation, and forbid unsupported absolute claims
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that performance evidence is an architecture test: tail growth and examined-document ratios often reveal boundary or modeling errors before functional correctness fails

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed stops at multiple systems, ownership boundaries, unbounded source discovery, or production traffic without objectives but does not explain MERN-specific splits across client, API, data, contracts, and deployment
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because parallelization by folder can separate React, Express, and database changes that form one invariant, while true deployment and rollback boundaries can be worked independently with explicit contracts

## Section 025: Future Refresh Search Queries
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed offers three broad theme queries that are likely to mix React, Express, Mongoose, MongoDB, TypeScript, security, and legacy tutorials without isolating a disputed claim or version
- **supporting_reason:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because claim-specific routing prevents high-ranking generic tutorials from crossing layer boundaries and makes actual guidance changes distinguishable from superficial ecosystem churn
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the broad stack phrase is used alone, search rank means authority, Mongoose and MongoDB results are merged, incompatible React or Express generations are mixed, or examples are copied without threat and data review
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 025 "Future Refresh Search Queries", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: use queries as research plans, not evidence before retrieval and inspection
